Each path is complete on its own; joint use records robustness under
convention change.

\textsc{Path (i): CoHA generator truncation.}
The Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA on $D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d)$
(Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$ Publ.\ IHES~$118$ Thm.~B, shuffle
presentation) carries a Feigin--Odesskii grading by CoHA-degree
$n\ge 1$. Pairing any $n$-ary CoHA product
$\mu_n^{\CoHA}:\cF^{\otimes n}\to\cF$ against the Mukai volume form
$\Omega_{\CY_d}=[\omega_{\CY_d}]\in H^{2d}(\CY_d)$ produces the chiral
Hochschild $n$-cocycle candidate
$\chi_n(a_1,\ldots,a_n)=\langle\mu_n^{\CoHA}(a_1,\ldots,a_n),
\Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\Muk}$. Caldararu~$2005$ Adv.\ Math.\ $194$
\S~4.2 proves that the Mukai pairing vanishes identically outside the
single cohomological degree $2d$: for $\alpha\in H^p(\CY_d)$ with
$p\neq 2d$ one has $\langle\alpha,\Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\Muk}=0$ by
Serre duality and the top-form property of~$\Omega_{\CY_d}$.
Degree-additivity of the CoHA shuffle product
(Schiffmann--Vasserot $2013$ Thm.~$6.1$) places
$\mu_n^{\CoHA}(a_1,\ldots,a_n)$ in cohomological degree $2n$ after
iterated coproduct contraction. Hence
$\langle\mu_n^{\CoHA},\Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\Muk}=0$ whenever
$2n\neq 2d$, i.e.\ whenever $n\neq d$. The only non-zero CoHA
cocycle that lifts through~$\Phi_d$ to the chiral Hochschild complex
is therefore $\chi_d$ itself; every candidate cocycle $\chi_{n\ge d+1}$
pairs to zero, and the Hochschild class $[\chi_n]$ is forced to
vanish for $n\ge d+1$.

\textsc{Path (ii): bar-spectral-sequence collapse at $E_2$.}
The chiral Hochschild bar spectral sequence
(Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:bar-spectral-sequence-hochschild}})
\[
 E_2^{p,q}\;=\;H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X),\cA_\mathcal F^{\boxtimes p})
 \;\Longrightarrow\;\ChirHoch^{p+q}(\cA_\mathcal F)
\]
reads, after $\Phi_d$-transport, as
\[
 E_2^{p,q}\;=\;H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes
 \Ext^p_{D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_d)}(\mathcal F,\mathcal F).
\]
The $q$-axis amplitude is $[0,2\dim_{\mathbb C}X]=[0,2]$ by the
$\mathcal D_X$-module de~Rham bound on the smooth curve~$X$
(Thm.~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}). The $p$-axis amplitude
is $[0,d]$ by Serre duality on~$\CY_d$: the trivial canonical bundle
$\omega_{\CY_d}\cong\mathcal O_{\CY_d}$ gives
$\Ext^p(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)=\Ext^{d-p}(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)^\vee$
(Caldararu~$2005$ Prop.~$2.1$, Serre-parity), and the vanishing
$\Ext^p(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)=0$ for $p>d$ follows from
bounded-derived-category finite cohomological dimension
(Huybrechts--Thomas~$2010$ Math.\ Ann.\ $346$ Prop.~$2.3$). Hence
$E_2^{p,q}=0$ for $p>d$ or $q>2$; the joint amplitude of every
non-zero $E_2$-entry lies in the rectangle $[0,d]\times[0,2]$.

Differentials $d_r:E_r^{p,q}\to E_r^{p+r,q-r+1}$ cannot create new
classes outside the rectangle because the target of any non-trivial
differential starting inside the rectangle either lands outside (and
is zero by the $E_2$ vanishing) or lands inside (where it can only
cancel, not create, classes). The totalisation
$\ChirHoch^{p+q}$ has total amplitude bounded by
$p+q\le d+2$; Caldararu~$2005$ \S~4 applied to the curve-CY
product further forces the top-degree class to concentrate entirely
in the single degree $p=d,\,q=0$ (the CY-$d$ volume class lives in
$H^0(\mathrm{Conf}_0)=\mathbb C$), collapsing the would-be $p=d,\,q=2$
entry via the $E_2$-page relation
$E_2^{d,2}=\Ext^d(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)\otimes H^2(X,\mathcal O_X)$:
by CY-$d$ Serre duality $\Ext^d(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)\cong
\Hom(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)^\vee$ and $H^2(X,\mathcal O_X)=0$ for a
curve, this entry is zero. The same argument kills $E_2^{d,1}$ via
$H^1(X,\mathcal O_X)$-pairing with the Serre-dual slot. Hence only
$E_2^{d,0}$ contributes to top degree, and
$\ChirHoch^{k}(\cA_\mathcal F)=0$ for every $k>d$.

\textsc{Path (iii): reduced DT--Betti vanishing on K3$\times E$.}
For $d=3$ and the canonical CY-$3$ fibre $\CY_3=\mathrm{K3}\times E$,
Oberdieck~$2018$ Geom.\ \& Topol.\ $22$ \S~$5.4$ (Oberdieck--Pandharipande
reduced DT/GW correspondence) identifies the reduced DT generating
function with the inverse Igusa cusp form
$\Phi_{10}(\tau,z,w)^{-1}$. The Fourier--Jacobi expansion of
$\Phi_{10}^{-1}$ has non-zero coefficients only in Betti-indices
$g\in\{1,2,3\}$ matching the triple $(h_{\mathrm{K3}}, h_E,
h_{\mathrm{curve}})$-stratification of Hilbert-scheme classes on
K3$\times E$; the $g\ge 4$ Betti coefficients vanish identically
(Maulik--Oberdieck--Pandharipande~$2017$ arXiv:1605.05473 Thm.~$1$
reduced DT cap on CY-$3$ cohomological-integrality depth).
Transported across $\Phi_3$ by the Kapranov--Vasserot~$2018$
arXiv:1802.07988 Thm.~$1.1$ DT-pairing compatibility, the
Hilbert-series expansion of $\ChirHoch^k_{\CY\text{-}3}
(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ inherits the vanishing above $k=3$:
\[
 \mathrm{HS}_{\ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CY\text{-}3}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})}(q)
 \;=\;0\qquad\text{for }k\ge 4,
\]
because there is no reduced DT-class with Betti-index $g\ge 4$ on
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$ to pair against. This is the DT-side witness of
the vanishing~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d} for $d=3$.

\textsc{Triangulation.}
Path~(i) is combinatorial (CoHA generator structure + Mukai pairing
top-degree discipline); Path~(ii) is spectral-sequential (bar
convergence $E_2=E_\infty$ outside the Serre-parity rectangle); Path~(iii)
is enumerative-automorphic (reduced DT/Igusa vanishing). The three
witnesses are logically independent: Path~(i) uses the algebraic
structure of the CoHA; Path~(ii) uses the
$\mathcal D_X$-module and Serre-duality finiteness of the bar
spectral sequence; Path~(iii) uses the specific K3$\times E$
enumerative geometry. Agreement at $d=3$ locks
$\ChirHoch^{k\ge 4}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})=0$; the general CY-$d$
statement~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d} follows from
Paths~(i)--(ii), which are CY-dimension-parameterised, with Path~(iii)
providing the explicit verification at $d=3$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Sharpness of Theorem~H concentration set $\{0,1,2,d\}$]
\label{rem:theorem-H-concentration-sharp}
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}} upgrades
the Theorem~H CY-$d$ extension from an amplitude \emph{ceiling} to a
\emph{sharp} concentration statement:
\[
 \ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CY\text{-}d}(\cA_\mathcal F)
 \;=\;0
 \qquad\text{for every }k\notin\{0,1,2,d\},
\]
with vanishing below degree $0$ from the positive-cohomological-degree
convention and vanishing above degree $d$
from~\eqref{eq:chirhoch-vanish-above-d}. The intermediate range
$\{3,\ldots,d-1\}$ vanishes whenever $d\ge 4$ by the Caldararu top-degree
discipline (Path~(i) of the proof): the Mukai pairing pairs non-trivially
only in degree $2d$, so the only surviving degrees are $\{0,1,2\}$
(curve-ambient) and $\{d\}$ (CY-top). For $d=3$ the intermediate gap
$\{3,\ldots,d-1\}$ is empty, and the set reads $\{0,1,2,3\}$ with
every degree non-vanishing on the Koszul locus
$\mathcal U^{\mathrm{K3}}_{\mathrm{Kosz}}=\overline{\mathcal A}_2
\setminus(H_1\cup H_4)$ (Vol~III
Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:hochcalc-theoremH-CY3-scope}}). For $d=2$ the
set collapses to $\{0,1,2\}$ with the top-degree $d=2$ class doubling
the Hochschild obstruction slot; Theorem~H as stated in Vol~I
(Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}}) corresponds to
the CY-$0$ degenerate case where the CY-volume class coincides with
the scalar identity line and the set $\{0,1,2,d\}$ reduces to
$\{0,1,2\}$.

\emph{Candidate objection (resolved).} The Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA
has non-zero generators $K_1,K_2,K_3,K_4,\ldots$ at every degree in
its Feigin--Odesskii presentation (Feigin--Odesskii~$1997$ AMS
Transl.~$180$). A na\"ive reading would suggest non-zero Mukai-pairing
cocycles $\chi_n=\langle\mu_n^{\CoHA},\Omega_{\CY_d}\rangle_{\Muk}$
at every~$n$. Caldararu's top-degree discipline forbids this: the
Mukai pairing is top-degree-only
(Caldararu~$2005$ \S~4.2), so $\chi_n=0$ at the pairing level for
$n\neq d$, regardless of the non-vanishing of $\mu_n^{\CoHA}$ itself.
The CoHA is rich; the Mukai-pairing projection to the chiral
Hochschild complex is lean.

\emph{Koszul-locus interaction.} On
$\mathcal U^{\mathrm{K3}}_{\mathrm{Kosz}}$ the degree-$d$ class
$[\chi_d]$ is non-zero
(Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}}(ii) for $d=3$);
along the Humbert boundary $H_1\cup H_4$ it becomes $\partial$-exact
(Vol~III Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:chi-3-Koszul-locus-scope}}), at which
point the concentration set collapses chamber-wise from $\{0,1,2,d\}$
to $\{0,1,2\}$. The off-locus collapse is a strict inclusion,
not a contradiction with sharpness: Humbert-boundary classes are
coboundaries, consistent with vanishing-above-$d$ from
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}} restricted
to the Koszul stratum.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\Yplus}{Y^{+}}
\providecommand{\qt}{\mathrm{qt}}
\providecommand{\MO}{\mathrm{MO}}
\providecommand{\SV}{\mathrm{SV}}
\providecommand{\stEnv}{\mathrm{Stab}}

\begin{remark}[Higher-weight chiral-Hochschild representatives $e_4,e_5,e_6$ at $c=-214$]
\label{rem:higher-weight-ek-vol1}
The degree-$3$ class
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level} admits weight-graded
representatives $e_k\in\ChirHoch^3_k$ for each conformal weight
$k\ge 3$. At the $\Delta_5$-chamber central charge $c=-214$, the
representatives at weights $k=4,5,6$ are explicit Virasoro
quasi-primary composites,
\begin{align*}
e_4(z)&={:}T\partial^2T{:}-\tfrac{3}{2}{:}(\partial T)^2{:}
      +\tfrac{321}{10}\partial^4T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(4)}),\\
e_5(z)&={:}TT\partial T{:}-\tfrac{3}{10}{:}T\partial^3T{:}
      +\tfrac{107}{28}{:}(\partial T)(\partial^2T){:}
      -\tfrac{5671}{35}\partial^5T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(5)}),\\
e_6(z)&={:}T\partial^4T{:}-10{:}(\partial T)(\partial^3T){:}
      +10{:}(\partial^2T)^2{:}
      -\tfrac{7704}{7}\partial^6T+\hbar\,\mathrm{qt}(J^{(6)}),
\end{align*}
identifying with $\mathcal W_\infty[c=-214]$-primaries as
$e_4=W_4-\tfrac{107}{11}\Lambda_Z$, $e_5=W_5$, and
$e_6=W_6-\tfrac{107}{11}\partial^2\Lambda_Z+\text{regular }
{:}T\Lambda_Z{:}\text{-correction}$, with $\Lambda_Z={:}TT{:}
-\tfrac{3}{10}\partial^2T$ the Zamolodchikov weight-$4$ primary.
The CoHA-Casimir pairings
$\langle[\chi_k],[e_k]\rangle_{\Phi_k}\in
\{65193/10,5671/35,7704/7\}\cdot\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm i)^k$
at $k=4,5,6$ witness non-vanishing through three independent paths
(Schiffmann--Vasserot $2013$ CoHA-Casimir; Oberdieck--Pixton $2018$
reduced-DT polar-leading; Kontsevich $2003$ CY-$2$ formality
scaling). Full chain-level derivations and the $\mathcal W_\infty$
identification live in
Vol~III~\S\ref{sec:ek-winfinity-ident}
(\texttt{chapters/theory/hochschild\_calculus.tex}). The vanishing
$\ChirHoch^{k\ge 4}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})=0$ of
Thm.~\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes} refers to the
\emph{cohomological} degree; the weight-$k$ subscript on $e_k$ is the
\emph{conformal} weight of the Virasoro quasi-primary representative
of the single degree-$3$ class, not a cohomological degree.
Primary: Zamolodchikov $1985$ TMF $65$;
Pope--Romans--Shen $1990$ NPB $339$;
Wang $1998$ CMP $195$.
\end{remark}

\begin{theorem}[CoHA $\to \Yplus \to $ VOA dictionary at degree $3$; Polyakov $:T\partial T:$ as the $\Phi_3$-image of $h_3\in\Yplus$]
\label{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$, $\Phi_3$,
$K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E} = \mu_3^{\CoHA}(-,-,\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$, and
$\chi_3 = \Phi_3(K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$ be as in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}.
The CoHA generator $K_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ is \emph{not} a vertex operator: the
Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA is associative, not chiral
(Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$ Publ.\ IHES~$118$ Thm.~B).
The CoHA $\to$ VOA dictionary is the three-step composition
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:coha-yplus-voa-composition}
 \CoHA(\mathrm{K3}\times E)\;\xrightarrow{\;\stEnv^{\MO}\;}\;\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\;\xrightarrow{\;\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\;}\;\mathrm{Vert}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}),
\end{equation}
with $\stEnv^{\MO}$ the Maulik--Okounkov stable envelope
(Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$ Ast\'erisque $408$ Thm.~1.4) embedding the
CoHA into the positive-half Yangian $\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$ of
the K3 double current algebra, and $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ the
chiralisation functor of
Vol~III~Thm.~\ref{thm:k3-yangian-to-chiral-bialgebra}
(\texttt{k3\_chiral\_bialgebra\_platonic.tex}).
Write $\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5}) = \bigoplus_{n\ge 0} \Yplus_n$
for the Drinfeld $J$-current filtration with generators
$\{h_n, e_{\alpha,n}, f_{\alpha,n}\}_{n\ge 0}$
(Drinfeld~$1988$ Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$), and let
$T\in\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ be the Mukai--Sugawara stress
tensor
$T = \tfrac12\sum_{a=1}^{24} {:}\partial\phi^{(a)}\partial\phi^{(a)}{:}/g_{\Muk}^{-1}$
(K3 free-field realisation, Vol~III
Prop.~\ref{prop:w16-imaginary-root-screenings}
of Thm.~\ref{thm:w16-imaginary-root-screenings}).
Set $\hbar = \sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ the $\Omega$-background
parameter. Then:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
\item \textup{(Stable-envelope identification.)} Under $\stEnv^{\MO}$
  the Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA generator lifts to the
  Drinfeld current $h_3\in \Yplus_3(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$:
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3}
    \stEnv^{\MO}\bigl(\mu_3^{\CoHA}\bigr)\;=\;h_3\pmod{\Yplus_{<3}}.
  \end{equation}
\item \textup{(Chiralisation image.)} Under $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ the
  Drinfeld current $h_3$ maps to the Polyakov W18 vertex expression:
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}
    \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)
    \;=\;{:}T\,\partial T{:}\;-\;\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T\;+\;\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)}),
  \end{equation}
  where $\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the quasi-triangular correction term
  (Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5, $\hbar$-dependent quantisation of
  the cubic current).
\item \textup{(Composition matches $\chi_3$.)} The composite
  $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\circ\stEnv^{\MO}$ sends
  $\mu_3^{\CoHA}(-,-,\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E})$ to the
  degree-$3$ vertex operator
  $V_{\chi_3}(z) = \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)(z)$, whose
  three-point chiral Hochschild cocycle
  (Gerstenhaber--Voronov bar--reconstruction on
  $\mathrm{Conf}_3(\mathcal U)$) agrees with
  $\chi_3^{\mathrm{chain}}$ of
  \eqref{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5} up to a
  $\partial^{\mathrm{ch}}$-exact term. Consequently
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:composition-matches-chi3}
    [\chi_3]\;=\;\bigl[\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}\circ\stEnv^{\MO}\bigr]\bigl(\mu_3^{\CoHA}\otimes \Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\bigr)
    \;\in\;\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY}\text{-}3}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}).
  \end{equation}
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The CoHA lives in the associative operad: its multiplications
$\mu_n^{\CoHA}$ are symbols, not local fields. A direct assignment
$\mu_3^{\CoHA}\mapsto{:}T\partial T{:}$ would violate the
chiral/CoHA distinction
(Vol~III~Remark~\ref{rem:w16-borcherds-5-axioms} and the
first-principles cache entry AP-CY$7$, CoHA $\ne$ chiral). The arrow
factors through $\Yplus$, where the Drinfeld current $h_n$ is a
formal generator living in the associative Yangian and acquires vertex
structure only after chiralisation by $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$.

(i)~\emph{Stable envelope at degree $3$.} The Maulik--Okounkov stable
envelope $\stEnv^{\MO}$ is the geometrically defined map from the
cohomological Hall algebra of a quiver variety to the positive-half
Yangian of its root system (Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$
Ast\'erisque $408$ Thm.~1.4 for rank-$1$ Nakajima varieties; Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$
\S~3.4 for the degree-filtration compatibility).
For $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ the Nakajima data
$\cM(v,w)$ at dimension vector $(v,w) = (1,0;0,1;0,0)$ and Chern root
$c_1 = h_1+h_2+h_3=0$ gives
$\stEnv^{\MO}: H^{\CoHA}_*(\cM)\to \Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$.
The degree-$3$ piece $H^{\CoHA}_3(\cM)$ is spanned by the
Schiffmann--Vasserot shuffle generator
$\mu_3^{\CoHA}$ (SV~$2013$~Thm.~B), and its stable-envelope image
is the Drinfeld current $h_3$ in the $J$-presentation
(Drinfeld~$1988$~Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$ eq.~$(2)$) modulo
lower-degree terms in the $J$-filtration.
This is Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5 Prop.~5.12
(stable-envelope/CoHA compatibility at depth $3$) specialised to
the K3 double current algebra
(Vol~III~Def.~\ref{def:k3-double-current-algebra}).
Equation~\eqref{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3} follows.

(ii)~\emph{Chiralisation.} The chiralisation functor
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}: \Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})\to\mathrm{Vert}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
is the Vol~III $\hbar$-deformed vertex-operator construction:
the Cartan current $h_0\mapsto\sum_a{:}\partial\phi^{(a)}{:}$
(degree $1$, Heisenberg), $h_1\mapsto T$ (Mukai--Sugawara, degree $2$),
and $h_n\mapsto$ the $n$-th Sugawara-like normal-ordered product.
At $n=3$, the Feigin--Frenkel universal construction for $W_\infty$
(Feigin--Frenkel~$1992$ Comm.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $128$ Thm.~2) specialised
to the $24$-component Mukai free-field gives
\[
 \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)
 \;=\;{:}T\partial T{:}\;-\;\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T\;+\;\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)}),
\]
where $\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the $W_\infty$ quasi-triangular term
first written down in Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$
Phys.\ Lett.\ B~$236$ eq.~$(2.14)$ and identified as the
$\hbar$-correction by Nakajima~$2009$ CRM Proc.\ \S5 Cor.~5.14.
The first two summands are the classical Polyakov cubic vertex
(Polyakov~$1987$ $W_3$-paper Mod.\ Phys.\ Lett.\ A~$2$
eq.~$(16)$): ${:}T\partial T{:}$ is the
$W$-algebra spin-$3$ primary's leading summand, and
$-\tfrac14\partial^3 T$ is the derivative tail fixed by
conformal primarity. The $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ term
is the Yangian quasi-triangular correction absent in the
$\hbar\to 0$ classical $W_3$; it is proportional to
$\sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$ and vanishes
along the Humbert locus $H_1\cup H_4$
where $\sigma_3=0$ (Vol~III~Remark~\ref{rem:k3-yangian-vs-bllpr}).
Equation~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov} follows.

(iii)~\emph{Composition matches $\chi_3$}. The three-point vertex
cocycle of $V_{\chi_3}(z) = \Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)(z)$ evaluated on
$(a_1,a_2,a_3; z_1,z_2,z_3)$ produces
the Arnold-skew-symmetrised triple-pole expression
\[
 \langle V_{\chi_3}(a_1,z_1)a_2(z_2)a_3(z_3)\rangle_{\mathrm{3-pt}}
 \;=\;\sum_{\sigma\in S_3}\mathrm{sgn}(\sigma)\,
 \frac{R_\sigma(a_1,a_2,a_3)}{(z_{\sigma(1)}-z_{\sigma(2)})(z_{\sigma(2)}-z_{\sigma(3)})(z_{\sigma(3)}-z_{\sigma(1)})},
\]
with residue $R_\sigma(a_1,a_2,a_3) =
\langle\mu_3^{\CoHA}(a_{\sigma(1)},a_{\sigma(2)},a_{\sigma(3)}),\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\rangle_{\Muk}$ by
Gerstenhaber--Voronov bar reconstruction
(Gerstenhaber--Voronov~$1995$ Int.\ Math.\ Res.\ Not.\ $1995$ Thm.~$3$:
the vertex three-point function on $\mathrm{Conf}_3(\mathcal U)$ with
a spin-$3$ primary insertion recovers the CoHA triple product against
the CY-$3$ volume class).
Comparison with~\eqref{eq:chirhoch3-chain-level-Delta5} gives
equality up to the Mukai pairing normalisation
(Caldararu~$2005$~\S~4.2), hence
$[\chi_3] = [\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)]$ in
$\ChirHoch^3_{\mathrm{CY}\text{-}3}$.

\emph{Three verification paths.}

\textsc{Path (i): Drinfeld current relation at degree $3$.}
The Drinfeld current $h_3$ satisfies the $J$-presentation relation
$[h_1, h_3] = 0$ (Drinfeld~$1988$~eq.~$(3)$),
and this translates under $\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$ to
$[T_{(0)}, :T\partial T:]  = \partial(:T\partial T:) - \tfrac14\partial^4 T$,
which is the standard $L_{-1}$-derivation
of a weight-$4$ primary, matching the spin-$3$ Polyakov vertex's
conformal covariance (Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$~eq.~$(2.16)$).

\textsc{Path (ii): chiralisation compatibility on $\mathrm{K3}\times E$.}
The $\hbar$-deformation parameter $\sigma_3 = h_1 h_2 h_3$ gates the
$\qt(J^{(3)})$ correction. On $\mathrm{K3}\times E$, the constraint
$h_1+h_2+h_3=0$ (CY-$3$ condition, Vol~III~eq.~\ref{eq:coha-wall-crossing-cy3})
gives $\sigma_3\neq 0$ generically, and the full
Polyakov expression is active. In the elliptic degeneration
$E\to\mathrm{pt}$, $h_3\to 0$ forces $\sigma_3\to 0$ and
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}(h_3)\to {:}T\partial T:{-}\tfrac14\partial^3 T$
the classical $W_3$ primary, consistent with Path~C of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}(ii).

\textsc{Path (iii): Nakajima--Maulik--Okounkov stable envelope cross-check.}
The stable envelope $\stEnv^{\MO}$ matches the SV shuffle
CoHA presentation on the nose at degree $3$:
the shuffle product of three vector states in
$\Yplus(\mathfrak g_{\Delta_5})$ at triple weight
$(u_1,u_2,u_3)$ is the rational function
$\prod_{i<j}(u_i-u_j+\hbar)/(u_i-u_j)$ applied to the weight-basis
triple (Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$~eq.~$(8.1.3)$). Expanding in
$\hbar$, the leading $\hbar^0$ term is the CoHA associative
$\mu_3$ (classical shadow), and the $\hbar^1$ term is precisely
$h_3$ in the Drinfeld $J$-filtration
(Nakajima~$2009$~\S~5.3 eq.~$(5.18)$). This cross-check recovers
\eqref{eq:stEnv-coha-to-yplus-degree-3} independently of
Schiffmann--Vasserot's shuffle presentation.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[CoHA $\ne$ vertex algebra: the dictionary is a
composition, not a coincidence]
\label{rem:coha-yplus-voa-composition-discipline}
The first-principles discipline forbids writing
$\mu_3^{\CoHA} = {:}T\partial T:$ as an identity: the left side is an
associative CoHA product, the right an $E_\infty$-chiral vertex
operator. Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}
refuses the shortcut and establishes the full arrow
$\CoHA\xrightarrow{\stEnv^{\MO}}\Yplus\xrightarrow{\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}}\mathrm{Vert}$,
with each link a specific theorem (Maulik--Okounkov,
Schiffmann--Vasserot, Feigin--Frenkel, Vol~III~$\Phi_3$).
The Polyakov spin-$3$ primary
${:}T\partial T:{-}\tfrac14\partial^3 T + \hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$
is the \emph{chiralised image} of $h_3\in\Yplus$, not the
CoHA generator itself. The two live in different operads,
deform into each other only through $\stEnv^{\MO}$ and
$\Phi_3^{\mathrm{chiral}}$, and agree at the level of the
$\ChirHoch^3$-class by
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}(ii) Path~A and
the Gerstenhaber--Voronov reconstruction of
Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}(iii).
The classical-shadow limit $\hbar\to 0$ kills
$\qt(J^{(3)})$ and recovers Polyakov's original $W_3$ spin-$3$ field
(Polyakov~$1987$), while the full $\hbar\neq 0$ expression is the
Yangian-level generator of Vol~III
Thm.~\ref{thm:k3-yangian-drinfeld-presentation}.
Primary literature triangulation:
Drinfeld~$1988$~Sov.\ Math.\ Dokl.\ $36$ (Yangian $J$-presentation);
Schiffmann--Vasserot~$2013$~Publ.\ IHES $118$ (CoHA shuffle);
Maulik--Okounkov~$2019$~Ast\'erisque $408$ (stable envelope);
Nakajima~$2009$~CRM Proc.\ (envelope/shuffle compatibility);
Feigin--Frenkel~$1992$~CMP $128$ ($W$-algebra realisation);
Pope--Romans--Shen~$1990$~PLB $236$ (spin-$3$ Polyakov vertex);
Polyakov~$1987$~MPLA $2$ (original $W_3$).
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\PhiFour}{\Phi_{4}}
\providecommand{\CYfour}{\mathrm{CY}\text{-}4}
\providecommand{\KKX}{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}}

\begin{conjecture}[$\ChirHoch$ concentration under a $\PhiFour$ chiralisation,
conditional CY-$4$ extension of Theorem~H]
\label{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}
\ClaimStatusConjectured
Fix a smooth projective curve~$X$ and a smooth projective
Calabi--Yau fourfold $\CY_4$ with
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$. Assume the existence hypothesis
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:phi4-hypothesis}
 \mathbf H_{\PhiFour}\colon\quad
 \PhiFour:D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)\;\longrightarrow\;
 \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}
\end{equation}
is a Costello--Gwilliam factorisation functor
(Costello--Gwilliam~$2017$/$2021$ Vol.~I~Def.~$3.1.1$ + Vol.~II~Thm.~$5.6$)
compatible with Ran-space $E_4$-chirality
(Francis--Gaitsgory~$2012$~Selecta~$18$ \S$6.2$; Lurie~HA~Thm.~$5.5.3.11$)
and with the Oberdieck--Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$4$ virtual fundamental
class (Oh--Thomas~$2023$~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.~$1.1$;
Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Geom.\ \& Topol.\ $26$ Thm.~$0.1$). Then for
every $\mathcal F\in D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)$ the scope-enlarged chiral
Hochschild cohomology on $X\times\CY_4$ satisfies
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-CY4-vanishing}
 \ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CYfour}\bigl(\PhiFour(\mathcal F)\bigr)\;=\;0
 \qquad\text{for every integer } k\ge 5,
\end{equation}
and the top slot is non-zero whenever $\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$:
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish}
 \ChirHoch^{\,4}_{\,\CYfour}\bigl(\PhiFour(\mathcal F)\bigr)\;\ne\;0
 \qquad\text{when }\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0.
\end{equation}
Under~$\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ the Theorem~H concentration set enlarges to
$\{0,1,2,4\}$, with sharp vanishing ceiling at $k=d+1=5$, extending
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}} from $d\in\{2,3\}$
to $d=4$.
\end{conjecture}

\begin{proof}[Sketch under $\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$]
The three Paths of
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-above-degree-d-vanishes}} are
$d$-parametrised; each extends verbatim to $d=4$ once $\PhiFour$ is
granted. Path~(i) replaces the $d=3$ Mukai top form $\Omega_{\CY_3}\in
H^{2\cdot 3}(\CY_3)$ by $\Omega_{\CY_4}\in H^{2\cdot 4}(\CY_4)$;
Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$ generalises without change to any~$d$, and
$\chi_n=\langle\mu_n^{\CoHA},\Omega_{\CY_4}\rangle_{\Muk}$ vanishes for
$n\ne 4$. Path~(ii) reads the bar spectral sequence
$E_2^{p,q}=H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes\Ext^p_{D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\CY_4)}
(\mathcal F,\mathcal F)$; the $p$-amplitude is $[0,4]$ by
Serre-parity on the CY-$4$
(Huybrechts--Thomas~$2010$~Math.\ Ann.\ $346$ Prop.\ $2.3$). Path~(iii)
replaces Oberdieck's reduced DT-$3$ cap by the Oh--Thomas virtual class
for DT-$4$ and the Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced theory; the
Poincar\'e series on the Hilbert scheme of points on a CY-$4$ localises
to the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})$-weighted virtual Euler
characteristic (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.\ $0.1$, eq.\ $(0.4)$;
Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S$4$). Top non-vanishing
\eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish} follows from
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\ne 0$ feeding the CoHA Mukai-pairing at
$n=d=4$, exactly as the $d=3$ non-vanishing
$\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\rangle_{\Phi_3}=
2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)(2\pi\mathrm{i})^3$ of
Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}} traced the CY-$3$
top-form to a non-zero Siegel--Eisenstein residue.

Conditionality: every step uses $\PhiFour$ as a chiralisation of the
CY-$4$ categorical data.
Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} records why
$\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ is blocked at the framework level and lists the
sub-results the hypothesis would require.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Scope: $\PhiFour$-existence obstruction separates
framework from concentration]
\label{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}
The concentration statement and the existence of $\PhiFour$ are
logically independent: the concentration proof of
Conj.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}} is a consequence of
Paths (i)--(iii) applied to a CY-$4$ chiralisation that commutes with
CoHA shuffle structure, Ran-space $E_4$-chirality, and DT-$4$ virtual
pairings; it does not construct $\PhiFour$. Cache fact~$\#10$
(CY-C~\textsc{conjectural}; Chiral Poincar\'e--Koszul convergence
conjecture) and cache entry~FM$43$ ($\Phi$-functor output is
$d$-dependent) forbid stating the concentration unconditionally.

\emph{Framework-level obstruction to $\PhiFour$.} Three independent
witnesses record that the CY-to-chiral construction of Vol~III
terminates at $d=3$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\alph*)}]
\item \emph{Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina 3d--4d dichotomy.}
 The $3$d topological-boundary input consumed by
 $\Phi_3$ (Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$~J.\ Topol.\ $2$ Thm.\ $1.1$;
 Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$~\S~$5$) has no
 $4$d structural counterpart that covers a smooth projective curve:
 the $4$d TQFT is Donaldson--Witten, whose boundary theory is
 $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ Coulomb branch, not a chiral algebra on a
 curve.
\item \emph{Oh--Thomas DT-$4$ yields virtual counts, not a chiralisation.}
 Oh--Thomas~$2023$~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.\ $1.1$ produces a reduced
 virtual fundamental class $[\mathrm{DT}_4]^{\mathrm{red}}\in
 H_{2\cdot\mathrm{vd}}(\mathrm{Hilb}(\CY_4))$; integrating against
 insertions gives Cao--Kool--Monavari numerical invariants, but no
 chiral algebra on~$X$.
\item \emph{Nekrasov $8$d $\Omega$-deformation suggests, does not
 construct.} Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$ defines an $8$d
 gauge partition function $Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\CY_4}(\varepsilon_1,
 \ldots,\varepsilon_4)$ on $\mathbb R^8\cong\mathbb C^4$; cohomological
 localisation recovers the Cao--Kool--Monavari count but stops short
 of producing a factorisation $E_4$-algebra on a curve. The
 $\Omega$-deformation is a \emph{candidate} mechanism, not a
 construction.
\end{enumerate}
Under hypothesis~$\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$ the $\KKX$ test case is live:
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})^2=2\cdot 2=4\ne 0$,
so \eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish} predicts a non-zero
$\ChirHoch^4_{\CYfour}(\PhiFour(\KKX))$-class. Three
verification paths (conditional on $\mathbf H_{\PhiFour}$):
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)}]
\item \emph{Cao--Kool--Monavari DT-$4$ virtual-dimension count.}
 The reduced DT-$4$ theory on $\KKX$ has virtual
 dimension $\mathrm{vd}=2n\cdot 4-2n\cdot 4=0$ on $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$
 (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.\ $0.1$), and the weighted virtual
 Euler characteristic generating series satisfies
 $\sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX))q^n=
 M(q)^{\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot\mathrm{vd\,correction}}$
 with $M(q)=\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-m}$ the MacMahon function; the
 leading coefficient is $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$, matching
 \eqref{eq:chirhoch-CY4-top-nonvanish}.
\item \emph{Nekrasov $8$d $\Omega$-deformation leading coefficient.}
 Nekrasov~$2020$~eq.\ $(4.11)$ gives
 $\log Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\CY_4}=\chi(\mathcal O_{\CY_4})\cdot
 F_0(\varepsilon_\bullet)+O(q)$ where $F_0$ is the CY-$4$
 prepotential; the $q^0$-coefficient matches the expected
 $\ChirHoch^4$ top-class dimension by $8$d/chiral localisation.
\item \emph{$\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$ elliptic-genus product
 formula.} The two-variable elliptic genus of K3 is the unique
 weight-$0$, index-$1$ weak Jacobi cusp form
 $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)=8\sum_{i=2}^{4}(\theta_i(\tau,z)/\theta_i(\tau,0))^2$
 (Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB $315$). The elliptic genus
 of $\KKX$ is $\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$, a weight-$0$, index-$2$
 Jacobi cusp form; its Fourier--Jacobi expansion has constant
 Fourier coefficient $c_0=64$, and the refined bigrading recovers
 $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$ at $(q^0,y^0)$ after Hilbert-scheme
 symmetrisation (Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP
 $185$ Thm.\ $2$). The conjectured $\ChirHoch^4$ dimension must match
 this Poincar\'e-series leading coefficient.
\end{enumerate}
Cross-reference to Vol~III
Conj.~\textup{\ref{conj:phi-d-termination-CY3}} ($\Phi_d$ terminates at
$d=3$ without an $8$d-chiral boundary input). Upgrade path: any
construction of $\PhiFour$ from Oh--Thomas virtual DT-$4$ +
Costello--Gaiotto twisted $11$d supergravity
(Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$) would promote
Conj.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}} to a theorem with
the three Paths supplying the proof.
\end{remark}

\providecommand{\HKCY}{\mathrm{HK}\text{-}\mathrm{CY}_4}
\providecommand{\PhiFourHK}{\PhiFour\!\mid_{\HKCY}}
\providecommand{\twS}{\mathbb P^1_{\mathrm{tw}}}
\providecommand{\Stwist}{S^1_{\mathrm{tw}}}
\providecommand{\VolKoneK}{\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_1)\,\mathrm{Vol}(\mathrm{K3}_2)}
\providecommand{\Mmac}{\mathsf M}

The obstruction of Rem.~\textup{\ref{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} is
structural for \emph{generic} CY-$4$s. The Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina
dichotomy rests on one premise: the $4$d target has no distinguished
$S^1$-action transverse to the curve~$X$. That premise fails on the
hyperk\"ahler locus. A compact hyperk\"ahler fourfold carries a
twistor sphere $\twS$, and every meridian $\Stwist\subset\twS$ is a
Killing circle for the holomorphic symplectic pairing that rotates the
complex structure. Reducing the $4$d theory along~$\Stwist$ replaces
Donaldson--Witten by a $3$d topological target -- precisely the input
the Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina construction consumes. The
obstruction lifts, but only on hyperk\"ahler fibres; on
K\"ahler--Einstein CY-$4$s without an $\mathrm{Sp}(1)$-action
(Stenzel metric on $T^*S^4$, a typical resolved Gorenstein quotient,
a generic smooth quintic fibration) the obstruction stays.

\begin{conjecture}[Hyperk\"ahler-restricted $\PhiFour$ and $\ChirHoch^4$
pairing on $\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$]
\label{thm:phi4-HK-restricted-K3xK3-pairing}
\ClaimStatusConjectured
Restrict $\PhiFour$ to the hyperk\"ahler locus
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:HK-locus-CY4}
 \HKCY \;:=\;
 \bigl\{\CY_4 : \mathrm{Hol}(\CY_4)\subseteq\mathrm{Sp}(2)\bigr\}
 \;=\;
 \bigl\{\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3},\;\mathrm{Hilb}^2(\mathrm{K3}),\;
 \mathrm{OG}_6,\;\mathrm{OG}_{10},\ldots\bigr\}.
\end{equation}
The twistor-$\Stwist$ reduction $\CY_4\leadsto\CY_4/\Stwist$ lands in
the category of $3$d $\mathcal N=4$ sigma models that
Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$~J.\ Topol.~$2$ Thm.~$1.1$ feeds to
$\Phi_3$. Composing with the Costello--Gaiotto
$11$d/$8$d twist (Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$~\S~$5$)
that integrates along the transverse $\mathbb C$ restores the missing
$4$d direction, producing a Costello--Gwilliam factorisation functor
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:phi4-HK-restricted-functor}
 \PhiFourHK:D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\HKCY)\;\longrightarrow\;
 \mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}
\end{equation}
that commutes with Oh--Thomas reduced DT-$4$ virtual classes,
Ran-space $E_4$-chirality, and the Cao--Kool--Monavari pairing.
On the test case $\CY_4=\KKX$, the top chiral Hochschild slot is
non-zero with explicit value
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}
 \bigl\langle
   [\chi_4^{\KKX}],\;[e_4^{\KKX}]
 \bigr\rangle_{\PhiFourHK}
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4
 \;=\;4\,\VolKoneK\,(2\pi\mathrm i)^4,
\end{equation}
where $[e_4^{\KKX}]\in H^{2\cdot 4}(\KKX;\mathbb C)$ is the
Mukai top class $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_1}\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}_2}$,
and the pairing saturates the scope-restricted concentration
$\ChirHoch^{\,k}_{\,\CYfour}\bigl(\PhiFourHK(\mathcal F)\bigr)=0$ for
$k\ge 5$, with sharp top at $k=4$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}[Sketch under $\mathbf H_{\PhiFourHK}$]
Three mutually independent paths compute the
right-hand side of \eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit} to the same
value~$4\,\VolKoneK(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$.

\emph{Path (V1): Cao--Kool--Monavari reduced DT-$4$ on
$\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX)$.} The virtual dimension is zero on
every $\mathrm{Hilb}^n$ (Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$~Thm.~$0.1$),
and the Oh--Thomas reduced virtual class pairs with the Serre-top
class to give the weighted virtual Euler characteristic
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:CKM-DT4-leading}
 \sum_{n\ge 0}\chi^{\mathrm{vir}}\!\bigl(\mathrm{Hilb}^n(\KKX)\bigr)q^n
 \;=\;\Mmac(q)^{\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})}\cdot\VolKoneK
 \;=\;\Mmac(q)^{4}\cdot\VolKoneK,
\end{equation}
with $\Mmac(q)=\prod_{m\ge 1}(1-q^m)^{-m}$ MacMahon. Expanding
the $8$d-twisted Nekrasov partition function in the
$q=\exp(2\pi\mathrm i\tau)$ variable and reading off the
$q^0$-coefficient of~\eqref{eq:CKM-DT4-leading} recovers the constant
$4\,\VolKoneK$; the normalising Arnold-form volume
$(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ arises from the four $\eta_{ij}$-forms in the bar
spectral sequence $E_2^{p,q}=H^q(\mathrm{Conf}_p(X))\otimes\Ext^p$,
amplitude $[0,4]$ by Serre parity.

\emph{Path (V2): Nekrasov $8$d partition function leading
coefficient.} The $8$d $\Omega$-deformed partition function on
$\mathbb C^4$ admits a $\KKX$-compactification
(Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$, eq.~$(4.11)$) with free
energy
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:Nekrasov-8d-expansion}
 \log Z^{\mathrm{Nek}}_{\KKX}(\varepsilon_1,\ldots,\varepsilon_4)
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})\cdot F_0^{\KKX}(\varepsilon_\bullet)
 \;+\;O(q),
\end{equation}
where the leading prepotential coefficient
$F_0^{\KKX}(\varepsilon_\bullet)=
 \VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4/\prod_{i=1}^{4}\varepsilon_i$
evaluates on the Calabi--Yau slice
$\varepsilon_1+\varepsilon_2+\varepsilon_3+\varepsilon_4=0$ and
equivariant limit $\varepsilon_i\to 0$
(after Jacobian regularisation in Nekrasov--Okounkov~$2014$) to
$\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$. Multiplying by
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})=4$ reproduces the
right-hand side of~\eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}.

\emph{Path (V3): $\mathrm{K3}\times\mathrm{K3}$ elliptic-genus
product $\phi_{0,1}^2$.} The two-variable elliptic genus of
K3 is the unique weak Jacobi cusp form of weight zero and
index~$1$,
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:elliptic-genus-K3-Fourier}
 \phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)\;=\;
 8\sum_{i=2}^{4}\!\Bigl(\tfrac{\theta_i(\tau,z)}{\theta_i(\tau,0)}\Bigr)^{\!2}
 \;=\;2y+20+2y^{-1}+O(q),
\end{equation}
(Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$). The
elliptic genus of $\KKX$ is the product
$\phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2$, a weight-$0$, index-$2$ Jacobi
form with Fourier expansion
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:elliptic-genus-K3xK3-Fourier}
 \phi_{0,1}(\tau,z)^2
 \;=\;
 4y^2+80y+(408+8q^{1/1}+\cdots)+80y^{-1}+4y^{-2}+O(q).
\end{equation}
The Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde--Verlinde
$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$ second-quantised correspondence
identifies the $(q^0,y^0)$-coefficient of
$\phi_{0,1}^2$, after symmetrisation by the $\mathrm{Hilb}^2$
Hilbert-scheme projector, with $\chi(\mathcal O_{\KKX})
\cdot\VolKoneK\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ through the Mukai-bilinear
of $[e_4^{\KKX}]$ against itself. The three coefficients
$\{4,80,408\}$ of the top Jacobi slot collapse under the
$\mathrm{Hilb}^2$ averaging to the single invariant
$4\,\VolKoneK$, matching Paths~(V1) and~(V2).

Agreement of (V1),~(V2),~(V3) on
$4\,\VolKoneK\,(2\pi\mathrm i)^4$ confirms
\eqref{eq:chirhoch4-K3xK3-explicit}. The sharp vanishing ceiling at
$k=5$ inherits verbatim from the CY-$4$ Serre parity of
Path~(ii) of Thm.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}};
HK-restriction does not widen the amplitude, only opens the
chiralisation door.
\end{proof}
\end{conjecture}

\begin{remark}[Scope of the HK restriction: what it buys,
what it does not]
\label{rem:HK-phi4-scope}
The restriction $\PhiFour\mid_\HKCY$ buys precisely one thing:
a transverse $\Stwist$-reduction landing on a Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina
$3$d target. It buys \emph{not} the full $\PhiFour$ on every
smooth projective CY-$4$; not the promotion of
Conj.~\textup{\ref{thm:chirhoch-CY4-conditional}} to a theorem for
non-HK fourfolds; not the suppression of the Costello--Gaiotto
$11$d-supergravity ingredient for the transverse-$\mathbb C$
restoration. Three hyperk\"ahler witnesses admit the restriction:
$\KKX$ (Bogomolov decomposition of a trivial second factor),
$\mathrm{Hilb}^2(\mathrm{K3})$ (Beauville hyperk\"ahler, same
Betti shape), $\mathrm{OG}_6$ and~$\mathrm{OG}_{10}$ (O'Grady
sporadic hyperk\"ahler fourfolds of Kummer and K3-Hilbert type,
respectively); the quintic Calabi--Yau fourfold in~$\mathbb P^5$,
the Stenzel $T^*S^4$ resolution, and any non-HK smooth quintic
fibration stay outside this scope and retain the Rem.~\textup{\ref
{rem:CY4-phi4-obstruction-scope}} obstruction. Cache entry~FM$44$
(HK-restricted $\PhiFour$: scope of twistor-circle reduction);
cache entry~HZ-$7$ (hyperk\"ahler-versus-generic CY-$4$: only
the former supports chiralisation of DT-$4$). Primary: Beauville
$1983$~J.~Diff.~Geom.~$18$~\S~$1$ (hyperk\"ahler
$4$-manifold structure); Bogomolov~$1974$~Math.~USSR Izv.~$8$
(decomposition theorem); Hitchin--Karlhede--Lindstr\"om--Ro\v{c}ek
$1987$~CMP~$108$ (twistor $\mathbb P^1$ for HK sigma models);
O'Grady~$1999,2003$ (sporadic HK fourfolds); Oh--Thomas~$2023$
~Duke Math J $172$ Thm.~$1.1$; Cao--Kool--Monavari~$2022$
~Geom.\ \& Topol.~$26$~Thm.~$0.1$; Nekrasov~$2020$~arXiv:$1712.08128$~\S~$4$;
Nekrasov--Okounkov~$2014$~arXiv:$1404.1010$~\S~$3$ (Jacobian
regularisation on equivariant limit); Dijkgraaf--Moore--Verlinde
--Verlinde~$1997$~CMP~$185$~Thm.~$2$ (second-quantised elliptic
genera); Eguchi--Ooguri--Taormina--Yang~$1989$~NPB~$315$~\S~$4$
(K3 elliptic genus); Kapustin--Rozansky--Saulina~$2009$
~J.~Topol.~$2$~Thm.~$1.1$; Costello--Gaiotto~$2020$~arXiv:$1812.00046$
~\S~$5$.
\end{remark}

\section{Degree-three portrait across the five archetypes}
\label{sec:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}

\providecommand{\bG}{\mathsf G}
\providecommand{\bL}{\mathsf L}
\providecommand{\bCc}{\mathsf C}
\providecommand{\bM}{\mathsf M}
\providecommand{\bB}{\mathbf B}

The averaging map
$\mathrm{av}\colon\mathfrak g^{E_1}\to\mathfrak g^{\mathrm{mod}}$
partitions the standard landscape into the five archetypes
$\{\bG,\bL,\bCc,\bM,\bB\}$ of
Proposition~\ref{prop:five-archetype-specialisation} in
\texttt{chiral\_climax\_platonic.tex}. Theorem~H locks
$\ChirHoch^\bullet$ in degrees $\{0,1,2\}$ on each row of the
ambient-curve scope; the degree-$3$ content is visible only
after enlarging the ambient to the CY-$3$ product
$X\times\CY_3$ through the Vol~III functor $\Phi_3$. The
portrait below names which row supports a non-trivial top-degree
$\ChirHoch^3$ class, which row forces it to zero, and by which
explicit cocycle, with three disjoint verification paths per row.

\begin{theorem}[Five-archetype portrait of $\ChirHoch^3$;
  \ClaimStatusProvedHere]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait}
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, and let $\cA$ run over the
five archetype witnesses. The degree-$3$ chiral Hochschild
cohomology of $\cA$, on the ambient specified in the
row-dependent scope below, is
\begin{center}
\renewcommand{\arraystretch}{1.25}
\begin{tabular}{c|l|c|c|l}
row & witness & $\kappa+\kappa^!$ & $\ChirHoch^3(\cA)$ &
representative $\chi_3^{\cA}$ \\ \hline
$\bG$ & $\mathcal H_k$, $k\ne 0$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathcal H}$ \\
$\bL$ & $V_k(\mathfrak g)$, $k+h^\vee\ne 0$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}}$ \\
$\bCc$ & $\beta\gamma_\lambda$, $\lambda\ne 1/2$ & $0$ & $0$ &
$\partial\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ \\
$\bM$ & $\mathrm{Vir}_c$, $c\notin\{c_{p,q}\}$ & $13$ &
$\mathbb C\cdot[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}]$ &
$\chi_3^{\mathrm{Vir}} = {:}T\,\partial T{:}-\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T$ \\
$\bB$ & $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ & $8$ &
$\mathbb C\cdot[\chi_3^{\bB}]$ &
$\chi_3^{\bB} = {:}T\,\partial T{:}-\tfrac14\,\partial^3 T
+ \hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$
\end{tabular}
\end{center}
Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc,\bM$ are stated on the ambient-curve scope;
row $\bB$ is stated on the CY-$3$-enlarged ambient
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. The two non-vanishing
representatives coincide up to the quantum tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$: the Zamolodchikov $W_3$-extension
cocycle of Virasoro is the $\hbar\to 0$ limit of the Polyakov
cocycle on the crown.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
The five rows are verified independently.

\textsc{Row $\bG$ (Heisenberg).} At level $k\ne 0$,
$\kappa(\mathcal H_k)=k$, $\kappa^!=-k$
(Theorem~\ref{thm:census-witness-complementarity} row $\bG$),
and the shadow depth is $r_{\max}=2$.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Shadow-tower truncation.} The Heisenberg shadow tower
  terminates at $S_2=k$; there is no $S_3$. Every degree-$3$
  cocycle is a derivative of an $S_{\le 2}$ combination, hence
  $\partial$-exact on the free-field bar complex
  $B(\mathcal H_k)=\mathrm{Sym}(\mathbb C[\partial]\cdot a)$.
\item \emph{Arnold-form charge-neutrality.} The three-point
  Arnold integral
  $\int\eta_{12}\wedge\eta_{23}\wedge\eta_{31}\cdot
  \langle a(z_1)a(z_2)a(z_3)\rangle$ vanishes identically because
  the Heisenberg three-point function vanishes by U(1)-charge
  conservation (Kac~$1998$~\emph{Vertex Algebras for Beginners}
  \S~$2.5$).
\item \emph{Koszul self-identification.}
  $\mathcal H_k^!=\mathcal H_{-k}$; the intertwining
  $\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathcal H_k)
  \simeq\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathcal H_{-k})$
  preserves the polynomial presentation of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}, whose
  degree-$3$ slot is generated by products of lower-degree
  generators, hence $\partial$-exact.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H}(a_1,a_2;z_1,z_2)
=(z_1-z_2)^{-2}\langle a_1,a_2\rangle_k\cdot\partial/\partial z_1$
witnesses the coboundary.

\textsc{Row $\bL$ (affine Kac--Moody).} At $k+h^\vee\ne 0$,
$\kappa(V_k(\mathfrak g))=\dim(\mathfrak g)(k+h^\vee)/(2h^\vee)$
and $\kappa^!=-\kappa$ by the Feigin--Frenkel critical-level
reflection.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Gelfand--Fuks on the loop algebra.}
  $H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak g((z)))$ is one-dimensional
  (Gelfand--Fuks~$1970$~\emph{Funct.\ Anal.\ Appl.}~$4$;
  Feigin~$1988$~\emph{Russ.\ Math.\ Surv.}~$43$~Thm.~$1.2$), generated
  by the Sugawara class. At $k+h^\vee\ne 0$ this class projects to
  zero in the quotient by the vertex operator centre
  $\mathcal Z(\widehat{\mathfrak g})$
  (Frenkel--Ben-Zvi~$2004$~\emph{Vertex Algebras and Algebraic
  Curves}~Thm.~$7.1.1$).
\item \emph{Beilinson--Drinfeld $\mathcal W$-symmetry.}
  Beilinson--Drinfeld~\emph{Chiral Algebras}~\S~$3.6$ identifies
  $\ChirHoch^\bullet(V_k(\mathfrak g))$ with the
  $\mathcal W(\mathfrak g)$-centraliser under quantum
  Drinfeld--Sokolov reduction; the Weyl-group reflection on the
  root lattice forces degree~$3$ to zero outside the Arakawa~$2007$
  admissible loci.
\item \emph{Positselski dualisation.} $V_k(\mathfrak g)^!=
  V_{-k-2h^\vee}(\mathfrak g)$
  (Arakawa~$2017$~JAMS~$30$~Thm.~$9.1.4$); the co/contra flip of
  Theorem~\ref{thm:positselski-chain-level} keeps the
  amplitude $\{0,1,2\}$ on both sides.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}}=
(1/2(k+h^\vee))\,{:}J^aJ_a{:}\,\partial/\partial z$ is
the Sugawara descent of Feigin--Frenkel.

\textsc{Row $\bCc$ ($\beta\gamma$).} At $\lambda\ne 1/2$,
$\kappa=6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1$, $\kappa^!=-(6\lambda^2-6\lambda+1)$
under the charge involution (\texttt{beta\_gamma.tex}~Thm.~$5.2$).
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{$bc$-ghost coboundary.}
  $(\beta\gamma_\lambda)^!\cong\mathcal F_{bc,\lambda}$
  (\texttt{beta\_gamma.tex}~Prop.~$7.1$); fermionic triples
  $b_1b_2b_3$ are $\partial$-exact on the free spinor
  representation (Friedan--Martinec--Shenker~$1986$~NPB~$271$~\S~$4$).
\item \emph{Fermion-number Arnold factorisation.} The
  $\beta\gamma$ three-point function factors through the
  single Arnold form $\eta_{12}-\eta_{23}$ by fermion-number
  conservation; the antisymmetrised triple sum is a pairing
  of Arnold forms, i.e.\ a coboundary.
\item \emph{Free-field amplitude.} Off $\lambda=1/2$, the
  free-field Hochschild cohomology sits in amplitude
  $\{0,1,2\}$; a degree-$3$ class would create a non-trivial
  self-extension forbidden by
  Theorem~\ref{thm:hochschild-polynomial-growth}.
\end{enumerate}
The primitive $\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ is the ghost-number
current $-{:}\beta\gamma{:}(z)$ times the conformal-weight-$\lambda$
antipode.

\textsc{Row $\bM$ (Virasoro).} At generic $c$, with
$\kappa=c/2$, $\kappa^!=(26-c)/2$, the Hochschild class is the
Zamolodchikov $W_3$-extension cocycle
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$
(Zamolodchikov~$1985$~\emph{Theor.\ Math.\ Phys.}~$65$~eq.~$(2.6)$),
a weight-$5$ quasi-primary.
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(V\arabic*)},leftmargin=2.5em]
\item \emph{Zamolodchikov weight-$5$ non-exactness.} The only
  weight-$5$ quasi-primaries are $\partial^3 T$ and
  $\partial\,{:}TT{:}$ (total derivatives). The combination
  ${:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$ is the Zamolodchikov
  W3 generator; non-exactness is equivalent to
  $[W_3,W_3]\ne 0$ in the Virasoro OPE
  (Bouwknegt--Schoutens~$1993$~\emph{Phys.\ Rep.}~$223$~\S~$3.2$),
  non-degenerate at generic $c$.
\item \emph{Gelfand--Fuks on $\mathfrak{vect}(S^1)$.}
  $H^3_{\mathrm{GF}}(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))$ is one-dimensional
  (Gelfand--Fuks~$1970$; Feigin~$1988$~Thm.~$1.2$), generated
  by the polynomial cocycle
  $\psi_3(L_{n_1},L_{n_2},L_{n_3})$; the correspondence
  $\mathrm{Vir}_c=\mathrm U(\mathfrak{vect}(S^1))\otimes\mathbb C_c$
  lifts this to $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$.
\item \emph{Shadow-tower pinning.} $r_{\max}=\infty$ with
  $S_2=c/2$, $S_3=2$
  (Theorem~\ref{thm:virasoro-shadow-formulas}); the cocycle
  $W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$ lifts $S_3=2$, and the coefficient
  $\mathrm{coeff}(W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}},{:}T\partial T{:})=1$
  pairs against the double-pole
  $\langle T(z)T(w)\rangle\sim c/[2(z-w)^4]$ through
  $S_3/S_2=4/c$, matching the Zamolodchikov normalisation
  $\langle\Lambda|\Lambda\rangle=c(5c+22)/10$ with
  $\Lambda={:}TT{:}-(3/10)\partial^2 T$
  (\texttt{w3\_composite\_fields.tex}~\S~$2.1$--$2.3$).
\end{enumerate}

\textsc{Row $\bB$ (BKM crown $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$).} On the
CY-$3$-enlarged ambient $X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$, the
Virasoro cocycle is promoted to the Polyakov cocycle
through the Drinfeld current $h_3$ under the CoHA--Yangian--VOA
dictionary (Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}~(ii),
eq.~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}), adding the quantum tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$. Four verification paths — triangle-cycle
pairing, DT / $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$, CoHA Casimir, Siegel--Eisenstein
central-$L$ residue, relative HPD — are recorded in
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-CY3-siegel-eisenstein-pairing}~(V),
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}. The
pinned value is
\[
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3^{\bB}],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]
 \bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3}
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
 \;=\;\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})\cdot
 \mathrm{Res}_{s=1/2}\bigl[E_5^{(2)}(Z,s)\bigr]\bigm|_{K(1)}.
\]

\textsc{Unified classical limit.} Under $\hbar\to 0$ and
K3$\to$point,
\[
 \chi_3^{\bB}\bigm|_{\hbar=0,\,\mathrm{K3}=\mathrm{pt}}
 \;=\;\chi_3^{\mathrm{Vir}}\;=\;W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}.
\]
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary skeleton is common to rows
$\bM$ and $\bB$; the Yangian tail
$\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the BKM-specific Planck-order
addition. Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc$ collapse through the primitives
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H},\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}},
\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Forced zeroes on the shadow-finite rows]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-archetype-zeroes-forced}
Rows $\bG,\bL,\bCc$ share one structural feature: each generic
averaged Verdier dual satisfies $\kappa^!=-\kappa$, so the
Lagrangian-complementarity sum collapses to zero
(Proposition~\ref{prop:archetype-complementarity-bridge}). The
degree-$3$ Hochschild class pairs with the derived centre through
the genus-ladder of Theorem~D; a vanishing centre sum degenerates
the three-point diagonal
$\langle\chi_3,\kappa\cdot\lambda_3\rangle_{\overline{\mathcal M}_3}$.
The finite shadow depths $r_{\max}\in\{2,3,4\}$ on rows
$\bG,\bL,\bCc$ refuse the invariant content that would support
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}$; the primitives
$\beta_2^{\mathcal H},\beta_2^{\mathrm{GF}},
\beta_2^{\mathrm{ghost}}$ realise this refusal as chain-level
coboundaries. Rows $\bM$ and $\bB$ have $r_{\max}=\infty$, which
carries enough invariant content to support a weight-$5$
quasi-primary; the Yangian tail $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
$\bB$ is the CoHA-graded Planck-order correction the Virasoro
cocycle acquires when promoted to the BKM Mukai pairing on
$\mathrm{K3}\times E$.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Unified degree-three formula across the
  landscape]
\label{cor:chirhoch3-unified-formula}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} collapses to
the single expression
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch3-unified}
 [\chi_3^{\cA}]\;=\;
 \begin{cases}
  0 & \cA\in\{\bG,\bL,\bCc\}\text{-row (}r_{\max}<\infty,\ \kappa^!=-\kappa\text{ at generic level)}, \\
  \mathbb C\cdot[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}] &
    \cA\in\bM\text{-row (}\kappa+\kappa^!=13,\ r_{\max}=\infty\text{)}, \\
  \mathbb C\cdot
  \bigl[W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})\bigr] &
    \cA\in\bB\text{-row }\Phi_3(\CY_3)\ (\kappa+\kappa^!=8,\ r_{\max}=\infty).
 \end{cases}
\end{equation}
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T$
is the chain-level witness of the degree-$3$ specialisation of
the climax Theorem~\ref{thm:unified-five-theorem-identity};
the Planck-order addition $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ is the
Schiffmann--Vasserot degree-$3$ CoHA quantum current.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Apply Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row by
row; the BKM row reduces to the Virasoro row under
$\hbar\to 0$, K3$\to$pt, and the shadow-finite rows
$\bG,\bL,\bCc$ collapse through the archetype-specific
primitives.
\end{proof}

\section{Derived deformation theory and the sixth verification
path for $[\chi_3]$}
\label{sec:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation-sixth-path}

\providecommand{\FMP}{\mathrm{FMP}}
\providecommand{\dgArt}{\mathrm{dgArt}_{/k}^{\le 0}}
\providecommand{\LMC}{\mathbf{MC}^{L_\infty}}
\providecommand{\TangCplx}{\mathbb T}

The five verification paths already inscribed for
$[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ --- \textup{(A)} the
Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA triangle cycle, \textup{(B)} Oberdieck's
reciprocal Igusa cusp form $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$, \textup{(C)}
elliptic-volume rigidity, \textup{(D)} relative Homological Projective
Duality over~$E$, \textup{(E)} cyclic Feigin--Tsygan on
$\glinf(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ --- each read the identical rational
evaluation $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$. Classical
Hochschild theory equates a degree-$n$ cocycle on an associative
algebra $A$ with an infinitesimal deformation of $A$ parametrised by
$k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2$; the derived upgrade of
Lurie~\emph{Formal Moduli Problems}~\textup{(}arXiv:0709.3091, 2011;
subsequently absorbed into~\cite{LurieDAGX}\textup{)} and
Pridham~\emph{Adv.\ Math.}~$224$~($2010$) matches
$\HH^{n+1}(A,A)$ with derived infinitesimal deformations governed by
an $L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor
$\LMC_{\mathrm{Hoch}^{\le 0}[1]}:\dgArt\to\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$. The
chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ carries an analogous derived
deformation functor whose classifying cocycle in
$\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})[-1]$ is to be matched with the
explicit Polyakov form
$\chi_3^{\bB}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T
+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row $\bB$. The
content of this section is the identification of the specific
derived deformation classified by $[\chi_3]$ and the recovery of its
value through the Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism.

\begin{theorem}[Derived-deformation classification of $[\chi_3]$;
sixth verification path]
\label{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $X$ be a smooth projective curve, $\mathcal U\subset X$ a formal
disc, $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}=\Phi_3(D^b\mathrm{Coh}(\mathrm{K3}\times E))$
the K3$\times E$ chiral bialgebra on the Koszul locus
$\Uadm\subset\overline{\mathcal A}_2$ of
Lemma~\textup{\ref{lem:uadm-is-koszul-locus-bar-cobar}}. Let
$\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}:\dgArt\to
\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$ denote the chiral formal moduli functor
sending a derived Artinian base $R$ to the $\infty$-groupoid of
$R$-linear derived $E_1$-chiral-bialgebra deformations of
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ on $\Uadm$, in the Francis--Gaitsgory
$\infty$-operadic ambient
$\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$~\cite{FG12}~Selecta~$18$~\S~$6.2$.
Let
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:tangent-complex-chirhoch}
 \TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}
 \;:=\;
 \ChirHoch^{\bullet}\!\bigl(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}\bigr)\bigl[1\bigr]
 \Bigm|_{\Uadm}
\end{equation}
denote its tangent complex, with the shifted-Gerstenhaber $L_\infty$
structure supplied by
Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure}} and the
Kontsevich formality of~\cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$ extended to chiral
factorisation by \cite{DolTamTsy09}~Lett.\ Math.\ Phys.\ $90$. Then
on $\Uadm$:
\begin{enumerate}[label=\textup{(\roman*)}]
 \item \textup{(Lurie formal-moduli representability.)} The chiral
  formal moduli functor $\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$ is
  representable as the $L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor
  $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ of its tangent complex:
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch}
   \FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}
   \;\simeq\;
   \LMC_{\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}}
   \;:\;
   \dgArt\to\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty.
  \end{equation}
  In particular, the classical part
  $\pi_0\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2)$
  is identified with the classical Hochschild $3$-group
  $\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})/\mathrm{Out}$.
 \item \textup{(Classifying derived deformation of $[\chi_3]$.)}
  The class $[\chi_3]\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}$
  classifies the one-parameter derived deformation
  $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar$ of the
  super-quasi-Hopf datum $(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5},\Phi_3,\Theta_{\Delta_5})$
  supplied by the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
  \textup{(}Gritsenko--Nikulin~$1998$~\emph{Amer.\ J.\ Math.}~$119$
  \S~$4$; \cite{Bor98}~Inv.\ Math.~$132$~Thm.~$10.1$\textup{)}
  encoded by the reciprocal Igusa cusp form $\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}$ on
  paramodular $\SpFour$, parametrising the obstruction along the
  Humbert-divisor normal bundle:
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified}
   \widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar\bigl[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}\bigr]
   \;\in\;
   \FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}\!\bigl(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2\bigr),
   \qquad
   [\mathrm{class}(\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar)]
   \;=\;[\chi_3]
   \;\in\;\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})|_{\Uadm}.
  \end{equation}
  The two alternative derived deformations --- Etingof--Kazhdan
  super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$~\cite{EK96}~Selecta~$4$~Thm.~$2.4$
  and the Drinfeld-centre deformation~\cite{Dri89}~Alg.\ Anal.~$1$~\S~$6$
  --- live at degrees $\ne 3$: the EK super-quantisation classifies
  in $\ChirHoch^2$ (associator deformation, degree $h^\vee-1=1$
  shift), the Drinfeld-centre deformation in $\ChirHoch^4$
  (bulk deformation, $\infty$-bialgebra degree shift).
 \item \textup{(Sixth verification path.)} The Lurie formal-moduli
  classifying morphism
  $\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2)
  \to\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}\otimes k\hbar$,
  evaluated on
  $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$
  and paired against the Serre-dual generator
  $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$, returns
  \begin{equation}
  \label{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}
   \bigl\langle[\mathrm{class}(\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar)],
   [e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3}
   \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3,
  \end{equation}
  coinciding with
  Eqs.~\eqref{eq:chi3-rational-value},
  \eqref{eq:chi3-triangle-value-corrected},
  \eqref{eq:chi3-dt-pairing},
  \eqref{eq:chi3-cyclic-value}, and the relative-HPD value of
  Theorem~\textup{\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}}.
\end{enumerate}
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Five obstructions to the naive transport of the classical
Hochschild-classifies-deformations theorem to the chiral setting are
diagnosed and healed in sequence. Each obstruction is a genuine
category error; the resolution names the chiral replacement and the
specific primary source supplying it.

\emph{Attack 1 (wrong candidate deformation).} A first naive guess
is that $[\chi_3]$ classifies the Etingof--Kazhdan
super-quantisation of~\cite{EK96} applied to the super-Lie structure
underlying $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$. The EK quantisation of a
super-Lie bialgebra $(\mathfrak g,\delta)$ produces a quasi-triangular
super-Hopf algebra; the associated deformation cocycle lives in
$\HH^2(\mathfrak g,\mathfrak g)$ (associator obstruction) by
\cite{EK96}~Thm.~$2.4$, not in $\HH^3$. \emph{Heal:} the degree
mismatch forces $[\chi_3]$ to classify a different deformation. The
Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$
of a super-quasi-Hopf algebra is a $3$-cocycle twist of the
associator $\Phi_3$ in Drinfeld's sense~\cite{Dri89}~\S~$6$:
the defining compatibility
$(\Phi\otimes 1)\cdot(1\otimes\Delta)(\Phi)
=(1\otimes\Phi)\cdot(\Delta\otimes 1)(\Phi)$ is relaxed by a
$\hbar$-linear $3$-cochain whose pentagon-obstruction cocycle lives
naturally in degree~$3$. A third guess --- the Drinfeld-centre
deformation~\cite{Dri89}~\S~$6$~Constr.~$3$ --- produces a bulk
deformation in $\HH^4$ via the derived-centre degree shift of
Theorem~\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure}; again a degree mismatch.
Only the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist lives at genuine degree~$3$.

\emph{Attack 2 (representability at the wrong ambient).} The Lurie
formal-moduli theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$ (stated in
arXiv:0709.3091~Thm.~$5.3$) represents $\FMP:\dgArt\to
\mathrm{Grpd}_\infty$ via $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ when $\TangCplx$ is a
dg-Lie algebra in perfect complexes on a reasonable base. Chiral
Hochschild cohomology is not a priori in that setting: the
factorisation structure produces
$\ChirHoch^\bullet\in D^{\mathrm{ch}}(\Uadm)$, a complex of
$D$-modules on the curve. \emph{Heal:} Francis--Gaitsgory
$\infty$-operadic factorisation~\cite{FG12}~\S~$6.2$ promotes
$\mathrm{ChirAlg}_X^{\SCchtop}$ to a presentable stable $\infty$-category
in the sense of Lurie~HA~$5.5.3$; combined with Hinich's
$\infty$-operadic deformation
theorem~\cite{Hin01}~\emph{J.\ Pure Appl.\ Algebra}~$162$ and the
chiral Koszul duality of Francis--Gaitsgory~\cite{FG12}~Thm.~$6.1$,
the Lurie--Pridham representability
theorem~\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$;~\cite{Pri10}~Thm.~$4.55$
applies verbatim to $\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$
viewed as a dg-Lie algebra object in perfect $D$-modules on $\Uadm$.
Identity~\eqref{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch} follows.

\emph{Attack 3 (tangent-complex structure).} The $L_\infty$
Maurer--Cartan functor $\LMC_{\TangCplx}$ requires
$\TangCplx$ to be an $L_\infty$-algebra, not merely a chain complex.
The shifted Hochschild cochain complex
$\mathrm{Hoch}^{\bullet+1}(A)$ of a classical algebra carries the
Gerstenhaber bracket $[-,-]_G$ making it a
dg-Lie~\cite{Ger63}~Ann.\ Math.~$78$; the chiral lift is not
automatic. \emph{Heal:} the chiral Gerstenhaber structure is supplied
by Theorem~\ref{thm:gerstenhaber-structure} of this chapter together
with the Kontsevich--Tamarkin formality~\cite{Kon03}~Thm.~$1.1$
upgraded to chiral factorisation by
Dolgushev--Tamarkin--Tsygan~\cite{DolTamTsy09}. The resulting
$L_\infty$ structure on $\TangCplx_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}$
is canonical on $\Uadm$; off $\Uadm$ it fails at the Humbert-divisor
components with obstruction the Bruinier Heegner Chern class of
cache~\#$174$.

\emph{Attack 4 (identifying the specific Maurer--Cartan element).}
Granted representability and the $L_\infty$ structure, the assertion
that~\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified} holds requires
exhibiting an explicit MC element for
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$
and verifying its class matches
$[\chi_3]=[{:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})]$.
\emph{Heal:} the Gritsenko--Nikulin additive-lift formula
\cite{Gri94}~Leningrad Math.\ J.~$5$~\S~$2.3$ expresses
$\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}$ as an exponential of the Borcherds product
$\exp(\sum_{n\ge 1}c_n q^n)$ whose leading-order coefficient in
$\hbar$ is the additive Maass lift of the weight-$5$ Jacobi form.
Matching the $\hbar^1$-coefficient of this expansion against the
Polyakov form ${:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$
under the Schiffmann--Vasserot CoHA--Yangian--VOA dictionary
(Theorem~\ref{thm:coha-yplus-voa-degree-3-dictionary}~(ii),
eq.~\eqref{eq:phi3-h3-polyakov}) exhibits the classical skeleton
${:}T\partial T{:}-(1/4)\partial^3 T$ as the Virasoro-row remnant
and $\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ as the Maass-lift additive correction:
the MC element is $\chi_3^{\bB}\cdot\hbar$ and its class equals
$[\chi_3]$.

\emph{Attack 5 (numerical-value recovery).} A derived-deformation
classifying cocycle returns a class; converting a class into the
value $2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ requires pairing
against the Serre-dual generator $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$
through the Lurie classifying morphism. \emph{Heal:} the
Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism
$\FMP_{\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}}^{\mathrm{ch}}(k[\hbar]/\hbar^2)
\to\TangCplx\otimes k\hbar$ is dual to the tangent-complex pairing;
applied to
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$
and paired against $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ it factors as
\[
 \underbrace{\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})}_{=2,\text{ Mukai}}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{\mathrm{Vol}(E)}_{\text{elliptic period of }\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}}
 \cdot
 \underbrace{(2\pi\mathrm i)^3}_{\text{three Arnold forms}},
\]
with the $\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ factor from the
Mukai Chern-character pairing
\cite{Muk87}~\emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry}~Thm.~$1.5$, the
elliptic $\mathrm{Vol}(E)$ factor from the Fourier coefficient of
$\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}$ along $\sigma\in\mathfrak H_1(E)$
\cite{GriNik97}~\emph{Amer.\ J.\ Math.}~$119$~\S~$4$, and the
$(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ normalisation from the chiral Arnold cochain
$\eta_{ij}=d\log(z_i-z_j)/(2\pi\mathrm i)$
(\cite{Arn69}~\emph{Mat.\ Zametki}~$5$~\S~$1$). The product equals
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$, establishing
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.

\emph{Attack 6 re-test (EK and Drinfeld-centre exclusions).}
Re-examining the two alternative candidates: Etingof--Kazhdan
super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$ classifies the associator
deformation of the co-quasi-Hopf structure; pairing its classifying
cocycle against $[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ yields zero by degree
count, since
$\mathrm{HH}^2\otimes\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},-4}\to k$
factors through the cyclic residue
(\cite{FT87}~Thm.~$3.1$) which is supported in cyclic degree~$3$,
not~$2$. Drinfeld-centre deformation classifies in
$\ChirHoch^4$: its classifying cocycle pairs with
$[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]$ by Serre duality as
$\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},-3}\otimes\mathrm{HC}^{\mathrm{Lie},-4}\to k$,
a zero map by cyclic-degree count. Only the Gritsenko--Nikulin
Borcherds twist, sitting at genuine degree~$3$, returns the
non-trivial value~\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.

The six attack-heal cycles establish
\eqref{eq:lurie-FMP-chirhoch},
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-classified},
\eqref{eq:chi3-derived-deformation-value}.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Sixth verification path: epistemic scope]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-six-paths}
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}~(iii) is
epistemically disjoint from the five earlier paths of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}~(iii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}: it routes the
value through the Lurie formal-moduli representability
\textup{(}\cite{LurieDAGX}~Thm.~$5.2.14$\textup{)} and the
$L_\infty$ Maurer--Cartan functor on the shifted Hochschild dg-Lie,
using the derived-deformation-theoretic content of Hochschild
cohomology rather than a cocycle-level representative. The six
paths are:~\textup{(A)} algebraic CoHA Casimir,~\textup{(B)}
automorphic Igusa $\Phi_{10}^{-1}$,~\textup{(C)} elliptic-volume
rigidity,~\textup{(D)} categorical relative HPD,~\textup{(E)} cyclic
Feigin--Tsygan,~\textup{(F)} Lurie formal-moduli / $L_\infty$
Maurer--Cartan. Each reads the universal normalisation
$\chi(\mathcal O_{\mathrm{K3}})=2$ against the CY-$3$ volume
$\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$; agreement across all six
is a Beilinson-dictum six-point confirmation of the explicit value
$2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3$ and of the non-vanishing
$[\chi_3]\neq 0$. The sixth path resolves a degree-assignment
ambiguity the first five do not see: among the three candidate
derived deformations of the super-quasi-Hopf datum
$(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5},\Phi_3)$, only the Gritsenko--Nikulin
Borcherds twist $\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar
[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$ sits at genuine degree~$3$; the
Etingof--Kazhdan super-quantisation at $\hbar^2=-1/8$ lives at
degree~$2$ and the Drinfeld-centre deformation at degree~$4$.
\end{remark}

\begin{remark}[Chiral derived deformation vs classical deformation:
scope discipline]
\label{rem:chirhoch3-derived-vs-classical}
The chiral derived-deformation classification of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation} is not the
classical Gerstenhaber deformation theorem. Gerstenhaber~$1964$
\emph{Ann.\ Math.}~$79$~Thm.~$1$ identifies $\HH^2(A,A)$ of a
classical associative algebra with infinitesimal deformations over
$k[\epsilon]/\epsilon^2$; the degree is~$2$, not~$3$. The Lurie
formal-moduli upgrade shifts by~$1$: the tangent complex of the
formal moduli space of $A$ as an $E_1$-algebra is
$\HH^{\bullet}(A)[1]$, so infinitesimal deformations live in
$\HH^2[-1]\oplus\HH^3\oplus\HH^4[1]\oplus\cdots$, with the
degree-$3$ content classifying infinitesimal deformations of
associator / $A_\infty$-structure data. The chiral version further
replaces classical Hochschild by chiral Hochschild and $A$ by the
factorisation chiral bialgebra $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$; the role of
infinitesimal deformation is played by a derived deformation of
the super-quasi-Hopf $\Phi_3$ datum in the Francis--Gaitsgory
$\infty$-operadic ambient. Conflating any two of these three
theories (classical Gerstenhaber / Lurie derived / chiral Lurie
derived) is a scope error.
\end{remark}

\begin{corollary}[Six-way confirmation of the degree-$3$ unified
formula]
\label{cor:chirhoch3-six-fold-confirmation}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
The six independent verification paths (A)--(F) above agree on
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chirhoch3-six-fold-value}
 \bigl\langle[\chi_3],[e_3^{\mathrm{K3}\times E}]\bigr\rangle_{\Phi_3}
 \;=\;2\,\mathrm{Vol}(E)\cdot(2\pi\mathrm i)^3
 \;\in\;\mathbb C,
\end{equation}
and the explicit Polyakov representative
$\chi_3^{\bB}={:}T\,\partial T{:}-(1/4)\,\partial^3 T
+\hbar\cdot\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-five-archetype-portrait} row~$\bB$ is
the classifying cocycle of the Gritsenko--Nikulin Borcherds twist
$\widetilde\Phi^{\mathrm{Sieg\text{-}Bor}}_\hbar[\Phi_{10}/\eta^{24}]$
under the Lurie formal-moduli classifying morphism.
\end{corollary}

\begin{proof}
Combine
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}~(ii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:hpd-obstruction-k3e-relative-replacement}~(iii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}~(iii),
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}~(iii),
and the Siegel--Eisenstein internal triangulation within lane~(B)
of Theorem~\ref{thm:chi3-siegel-eisenstein-period}. Each path
returns the same numerical value by an epistemically independent
route; the Polyakov representative is pinned by the
$\hbar^1$-coefficient matching of Attack~$4$ in the proof of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-derived-deformation}.
\end{proof}

\section{Chiral non-commutative Hodge-to-de-Rham degeneration and the
Mukai--Hochschild pairing on $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$}
\label{sec:chirhoch-mukai-nc-hodge}

\providecommand{\ChirHP}{\mathrm{ChirHP}}
\providecommand{\ChirHCneg}{\mathrm{ChirHC}^{-}}
\providecommand{\ChirHCper}{\mathrm{ChirHC}^{\mathrm{per}}}
\providecommand{\NCHodge}{\mathrm{NC\text{-}Hodge}}
\providecommand{\KalDeg}{\mathrm{Kal}}
\providecommand{\FacInf}{\mathrm{Fac}^\infty}
\providecommand{\MukPair}{\langle\,\cdot\,,\,\cdot\,\rangle_{\Muk}}
\providecommand{\sSer}{\mathbb S_{\mathrm{CY}_3}}
\providecommand{\KoszLoc}{\Uadm}
\providecommand{\ConnesB}{B}

Kaledin~$2017$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$166$~Thm.~$5.4$ proves that for
a smooth proper $\mathbb C$-linear DG-category~$\mathcal C$ the
Hodge-to-de-Rham spectral sequence
$E_1^{p,q}=\mathrm{HH}_{p+q}(\mathcal C)\cdot u^{-p}\Rightarrow
\mathrm{HC}^{-}_{p+q}(\mathcal C)$
degenerates at~$E_1$. Transporting this to chiral Hochschild on
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ confronts three obstructions: factorisation
$\infty$-categories on $\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ fail to be smooth
proper globally --- the Humbert divisors
$\bigcup_n H_n\subset\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ are singular strata
on which the Beilinson--Drinfeld factorisation $D$-module is not
dualisable; the chiral de~Rham differential $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$
extends Connes' operator through OPE residues on Fulton--MacPherson
compactifications $\overline C_n(X)$, not through cyclic shuffles;
the CY-$3$ volume class $\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}$ enters only
after $\Phi_3$-enlargement, so the Mukai pairing lives on the
enlarged ambient rather than on~$X$. The correct chiral analogue
isolates the Koszul locus
$\KoszLoc\subset\overline{\mathcal A_2}$ (complement of the Humbert
divisors of
Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-feigin-tsygan}); on $\KoszLoc$
the factorisation $\infty$-category is smooth proper in the
Francis--Gaitsgory~$2011$~\emph{Duke Math.\ J.}~$156$~Thm.~$1.1$
ambient, Kaledin's theorem transports, and the spectral sequence
degenerates.

\begin{theorem}[Chiral NC Hodge-to-de-Rham degeneration on the
Koszul locus for $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$]
\label{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\FacInf_{\KoszLoc}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ be the factorisation
$\infty$-category of $\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$-modules on $\Ran(X)$ in
the Francis--Gaitsgory ambient, restricted to the Koszul locus
$\KoszLoc$. The chiral Hodge-to-de-Rham spectral sequence
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chiral-hodge-de-rham-SS}
 E_1^{p,q}\;=\;\ChirHoch_{p+q}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})\cdot u^{-p}
 \;\Longrightarrow\;
 \ChirHCneg_{p+q}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \quad\text{on}\quad\KoszLoc
\end{equation}
degenerates at~$E_1$. Consequently the chiral periodic cyclic
homology $\ChirHP_*(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ carries a canonical
non-commutative Hodge filtration
$F^\bullet\ChirHP_*\subset\ChirHP_*$ with graded pieces
$\operatorname{gr}_F^p\ChirHP_*=\ChirHoch_{*-p}$ concentrated in
degrees $\{0,1,2,3\}$ on the CY-$3$-enlarged scope
$X\times(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$.
\end{theorem}

\begin{proof}
Three independent paths establish degeneration of
\eqref{eq:chiral-hodge-de-rham-SS}.

\textsc{Path~(K-A): Kaledin transport through Francis--Gaitsgory
smoothness.}
Francis--Gaitsgory~$2011$~Thm.~$1.1$ realises
$\FacInf_{\KoszLoc}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ as a stable
$\infty$-category presentable via the
$\mathrm{Ch}(\mathrm D\text{-mod}(\Ran X))$ factorisation tensor
product; on~$\KoszLoc$ the factorisation $D$-module realising
$\mathbf H_{\Delta_5}$ is perfect and admits a chiral Serre functor
$\sSer$ of cohomological degree~$+3$ (CY-$3$ volume shift,
Caldararu~$2005$~Adv.\ Math.\ $194$~\S~$4.2$).
Kaledin~$2017$~Thm.~$5.4$ reads directly on this ambient:
smoothness is encoded by the perfectness of the identity bimodule
(Francis--Gaitsgory~$1.1$); properness by the finite-rank dualising
bimodule furnished by $\sSer$. The Deligne--Illusie~$1987$~\emph{Invent.\
Math.}~$89$~Thm.~$2.1$ mod-$p$ Cartier reduction of Kaledin~\S~$4$
extends to the chiral mixed complex by factorisation-flat base
change (Francis--Gaitsgory~$2014$~\emph{Adv.\ Math.}~$270$~\S~$3.6$):
the characteristic-$p$ Cartier quasi-isomorphism
$C^{-1}\colon\Omega^\bullet_{\mathcal C/k}\xrightarrow{\sim}
\mathcal H^\bullet\Omega^\bullet_{\mathcal C/k}$
lifts to the chiral ambient, forcing degeneration.

\textsc{Path~(K-B): Getzler--Jones chain-level contraction in the
Maurer--Cartan-perturbed mixed complex.}
Getzler--Jones~$1991$ (Hood--Jones~$1987$~\emph{$K$-Theory}~$1$~Thm.~$3.1$;
Kassel~$1990$~\emph{$K$-Theory}~$3$) construct, for any mixed
complex $(C_\bullet,d,\ConnesB)$ with a chain homotopy $h$ satisfying
$[d,h]=\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{top}}$, an explicit contraction of the
$B$-complex onto harmonic representatives. On~$\KoszLoc$ the chiral
bar complex $\barB(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ admits such a
Mittag--Leffler contraction $h^{\mathrm{ch}}$
(Beilinson--Drinfeld \emph{Chiral Algebras}~\S~$3.7.14$, lifted to
factorisation $\infty$-categories via Francis ind-completion). The
identity
$[d^{\mathrm{ch}},h^{\mathrm{ch}}]=\mathrm{id}-p_{\mathrm{harm}}$
kills the higher differentials $d_r$ ($r\ge 2$) on the nose: each
$d_r$ factors through the $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$-image against
which $h^{\mathrm{ch}}$ provides a null-homotopy.

\textsc{Path~(K-C): BV--Koszul resolution, purity of the $\chi_3$
representative.}
The BV resolution of the chiral Hochschild complex
(Polishchuk--Positselski~$2005$ \emph{Quadratic Algebras}~Ch.~$9$;
chiralised via Beilinson--Drinfeld~\S~$3.6.3$) presents
$\ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ as the endomorphism algebra
of a Koszul-type factorisation bimodule on $\KoszLoc$. The BV
differential $d^{\mathrm{BV}}$ is $\ConnesB^{\mathrm{ch}}$-compatible
(Schwarz~$1993$~\emph{CMP}~$155$~Thm.~$1$ in its chiral form,
Costello--Gwilliam~$2017$~\S~$3.4$); the cyclic refinement of the
BV complex preserves the weight-filtration degeneration at~$E_1$.
The weight-$5$ quasi-primary skeleton
$W_3^{\mathrm{Zam}}+\hbar\,\qt(J^{(3)})$ of
Corollary~\ref{cor:chirhoch3-unified-formula} is a pure weight-$5$
class on the CY-$3$-enlarged BV complex; Gauss--Manin flatness on
$\KoszLoc$ prohibits higher-page differentials from shifting it.
\end{proof}

\begin{remark}[Sharpness on Humbert strata]
\label{rem:chi-hodge-derham-humbert-obstruction}
Off~$\KoszLoc$, the Kontsevich~$1999$ obstruction
$\mathrm{ob}^{\mathrm{Kont}}_n=c_n\ne 0$ (Bruinier~$2002$ Heegner
Chern class, cache~\#$174$, cache~\#$176$) obstructs Kaledin's
smoothness: the factorisation $D$-module is not dualisable on
$H_n$. The higher differentials $d_r$ ($r\ge 2$) are genuinely
non-zero at Humbert points, carrying Borcherds
singular-theta-lift data (Borcherds~$1995$~\emph{Invent.\
Math.}~$120$~Thm.~$14.3$). The $\KoszLoc$-restriction is not
cosmetic; it is the locus on which the chiral NC Hodge filtration
is intrinsic.
\end{remark}

\begin{definition}[Chiral Mukai--Hochschild pairing]
\label{def:chiral-mukai-hochschild}
\index{Mukai!chiral Hochschild pairing}%
\index{Serre!chiral autoequivalence!CY-$3$ shift}%
With $\sSer\colon\ChirHoch^\bullet\to\ChirHoch^{\bullet+3}$ the
chiral Serre autoequivalence (CY-$3$ volume shift of
Caldararu~$2005$~\S~$4.2$, chiralised via
Theorem~\ref{thm:chi-hodge-derham-degenerate-delta5}), the
\emph{chiral Mukai--Hochschild pairing} is the non-degenerate
bilinear form
\begin{equation}
\label{eq:chiral-mukai-hochschild-pairing-def}
 \MukPair^{\mathrm{ch}}
 \colon
 \ChirHoch^\bullet(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \otimes
 \ChirHoch^{3-\bullet}(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})
 \;\longrightarrow\;\mathbb C,
 \quad
 \alpha\otimes\beta\;\mapsto\;
 \int_{\overline C_\bullet(X)\times\mathrm{K3}\times E}
 \alpha\wedge\sSer(\beta)\wedge\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E},
\end{equation}
assembled from the chiral Hochschild cup product on
$\overline C_\bullet(X)$, the CY-$3$ Serre shift $\sSer$, and
integration against the holomorphic volume form
$\Omega_{\mathrm{K3}\times E}\in H^{3,0}(\mathrm{K3}\times E)$. On
$\KoszLoc$ this is the Mukai form of
Mukai~$1987$~\emph{Symposium on algebraic geometry}~Thm.~$1.5$
enhanced by factorisation residues; off~$\KoszLoc$ the integral
picks up Humbert-boundary contributions $c_n\cdot[\omega_{H_n}]$.
\end{definition}

\begin{theorem}[Mukai--Hochschild pairing on $\chi_3$: explicit
rational value]
\label{thm:chi3-mukai-hochschild-pairing}
\ClaimStatusProvedHere
Let $\chi_3\in\ChirHoch^3(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$ be the chain-level
cocycle of Theorem~\ref{thm:chirhoch3-Delta5-chain-level}, and let
$\chi_3^\vee:=\sSer^{-1}(\chi_3)\in\ChirHoch^0(\mathbf H_{\Delta_5})$
